\nt In February 2010 NA and BP decided to break down spatial and
temporal adverbs/relational nouns into their composite parts. For
a large part, this means defining a root which does not exist by
itself, but which can be identified in many case-marked forms.

whether it's a local word; the onomatopoetics fits quite well,
though

\lx erek
\a ere
\a er
\a e
\a u
\a oro
\ps pron
\ge prox
\nt Proximal demonstrative. The
full form is used in the
Nominative; the form in ere is
used in the Accusative (ere-w),
Instrumental (ere-ch),
Allative-Locative (ere-kle),
Allative-Prolative (ere-kli); the
form in er is used in the
Comitative (er-n'un), Allative
(er-teki), Elative (er-gich), and
Similative (er-gechin); the most
reduced form e is used in the
Dative (e-du), Locative (e-le),
Prolative (e-li), and Ablative
(e-duk).
\nt Proximal demonstrative. The full form is used in the Nominative;
the form in ere is used in the Accusative (ere-w), Instrumental
(ere-ch), Allative-Locative (ere-kle), Allative-Prolative (ere-kli); the
form in er is used in the Comitative (er-n'un), Allative (er-teki),
Elative (er-gich), and Similative (er-gechin); the most reduced
form e is used in the Dative (e-du), Locative (e-le), Prolative (e-li),
and Ablative (e-duk). In February 2010 we decided that the spatial
adverbs eweski 'ahead, to here' and ewgile 'this side/closer' are
probably derived from erek - perhaps with some 'contamination'
from aw- 'where'? So we glossed them accordingly
\dt 03/Mar/2012

\lx hilu
\a ilu
\ps vb
\ge drink
\nt In Kamchatka the form is ilu,
the standard form is hilu:; this
means to drink hot beverages
(and soup/broth); there is
another verb kol that means to

vodka), at least in Kamchatka
\nt In Kamchatka the form is ilu, the standard form is hilu:; this
means to drink hot beverages (and soup/broth); there is another
verb kol that means to drink cold beverages (water, vodka), at
least in Kamchatka

\lx h·ªãnma
\ps v
\ge choose
\a ·ªãnma
\a ·ªãmma
\ps n, adj
\ge speed
\ge fast
\nt The standard form begins with
a h-, and Cincius writes it with
an initial soft diphthong;
however, Rima Maksimovna
definitely did not pronounce
any initial glide. Interestingly,
in Sebjan they also pronounced
it without any initial
pharyngeal h-, but with a
geminated consonant.
\nt The standard form begins with a h-, and Cincius writes it with an
initial soft diphthong; however, Rima Maksimovna definitely did
not pronounce any initial glide. Interestingly, in Sebjan they also
pronounced it without any initial pharyngeal h-, but with a
geminated consonant.
